  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_29f4b300-85ee-4a9a-8219-9bbee636ae19'

<span id="freeTextContainer4599304174456793524">Tome I de II.<br/><br/>« On fit encore quatre ou cinq pas en montant toujours, puis Dantès sentit qu'on le prenait par la tête et par les pieds et qu'on le balançait.<br/>« Une, dirent les fossoyeurs.<br/>- Deux.<br/>- Trois ! »<br/>En même temps, Dantès se sentit lancé, en effet, dans un vide énorme, traversant les airs comme un oiseau blessé, tombant, tombant toujours avec une épouvante qui lui glaça</span>
  <span id="freeText4599304174456793524" style="display:none">Tome I de II.<br /><br />« On fit encore quatre ou cinq pas en montant toujours, puis Dantès sentit qu'on le prenait par la tête et par les pieds et qu'on le balançait.<br />« Une, dirent les fossoyeurs.<br />- Deux.<br />- Trois ! »<br />En même temps, Dantès se sentit lancé, en effet, dans un vide énorme, traversant les airs comme un oiseau blessé, tombant, tombant toujours avec une épouvante qui lui glaçait le cœur. Quoique tiré en bas par quelque chose de pesant qui précipitait son vol rapide, il lui sembla que cette chute durait un siècle. Enfin, avec un bruit épouvantable, il entra comme une flèche dans une eau glacée qui lui fit pousser un cri, étouffé à l'instant même par l'immersion. Dantès avait été lancé dans la mer, au fond de laquelle l'entraînait un boulet de trente-six attaché à ses pieds.La mer est le cimetière du château d'If. »</span>
  <a data-text-id="4599304174456793524" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1811507792" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13518197903744567765">In the annals of revenge stories, The Count of Monte Cristo has to be at the very top. The betrayal, imprisonment, reappropriation of identity and the final stroke of revenge are so perfectly depicted here that it is breathtaking. Dumas' finest work (besides the d'Artagnan cycle in my humble opinion), there is ne'er a dull moment in this classic of epic proportions.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3018676625&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3018676625" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3924024996550785153">I really wish I could give this a better rating.<br/><br/>I grew up French, and this was one of the stories I learned young. I figured I'd reconnect and read the actual novel after finding it for $7 in a book store.<br/><br/>But holy hell did I struggle to finish it.<br/><br/>The first third or so is all set-up. That's not too bad, pretty normal even. There are a lot of characters thrown at you early on, and it can be a bit tough to get them all straight.<br/><br/>Then Edmond gets thrown in jail. Now we're talking! There's some bleak </span>
  <span id="freeText3924024996550785153" style="display:none">I really wish I could give this a better rating.<br /><br />I grew up French, and this was one of the stories I learned young. I figured I'd reconnect and read the actual novel after finding it for $7 in a book store.<br /><br />But holy hell did I struggle to finish it.<br /><br />The first third or so is all set-up. That's not too bad, pretty normal even. There are a lot of characters thrown at you early on, and it can be a bit tough to get them all straight.<br /><br />Then Edmond gets thrown in jail. Now we're talking! There's some bleak stuff here, some serious introspection, and great insight into the mindset of a wrongfully committed man thrown into solitary confinement. <br /><br />Everything between Edmond landing in le Château d'If and him finding the treasure is fantastic. The language is great as is the story.<br /><br />But when he becomes the Comte de Monte-Cristo?<br /><br />You're looking at about 500 pages of setup for the next book. Nothing really happens. You're meeting all the pieces that you know will play a role in Edmond's revenge.<br /><br />BUT NOTHING HAPPENS.<br /><br />I'm going to take some time off before I jump into Part 2 because I really had to fight to get through this and I need a break.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3924024996550785153" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText784668953628884976" style="display:none">Honestly, this book has been a nightmare to read... and thank god it’s over. I’ve heard about it before and I thought it would be interesting??? It’s really not. The beginning was alright and actually not a pain to read, but when we got to the end, I actually started skimming through the pages just to get it over with. And there was absolutely no vengeance whatsoever... WHAT?? It’s a vengeance story with no vengeance (which was one of the things I was looking forward to). So yeah, unless it’s the beginning, it’s not worth going till the end. I hope the second one is better than that one.</span>

<div id="review_947722434" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/947722434" />
    <a title="Czarny Pies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29160274-czarny-pies"><img alt="Czarny Pies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1400687408p2/29160274.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/947722434?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Czarny Pies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Czarny Pies" href="/user/show/29160274-czarny-pies">Czarny Pies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29160274-czarny-pies?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29160274-czarny-pies?shelf=french-lit">french-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer947722434" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14852617493222649673">In order to enjoy the Comte of Monte-Cristo has the potential to profoundly irritate the reader of the twenty-first century in a number of different ways. First, it was written in serial form which means that the reader is constantly being reminded of things that would have occurred in episodes published three months or more previously which can be distraction for the modern reader who would likely have read the section with the event within the previous two or three days. Second, because Dumas </span>
  <span id="freeText14852617493222649673" style="display:none">In order to enjoy the Comte of Monte-Cristo has the potential to profoundly irritate the reader of the twenty-first century in a number of different ways. First, it was written in serial form which means that the reader is constantly being reminded of things that would have occurred in episodes published three months or more previously which can be distraction for the modern reader who would likely have read the section with the event within the previous two or three days. Second, because Dumas was paid by the word, there are many passages that run on for too long. <br /><br />However, the Comte of Monte-Cristo is long above all because it is very complex containing a great many sub-plots that are well-structured and well executed. In this context, the reader is highly grateful for the reminders that exist because of the work was originally a serial. Although, there a number of passages that appear to be verbose primarily for pecuniary reasons, the Comte of Monte-Cristo is the work where Dumas exercised the greatest discipline. It is without doubt his finest work.<br /><br />Readers are attracted to the basic premise of the novel. Edmund Dantes an honest young man is betrayed and sentenced to life imprisonment in the early 1820s. He is befriended by a fellow prisoner who tells him of buried treasure on the Island of Monte-Cristo. The Abbe dies. Dantes escapes from prison, finds the treasure and then spends another ten years amassing an even larger fortune.<br /><br />In the late 1830s, Dantes arrives in Paris with the a new alter ego and immense financial resources at his disposal to wreck his revenge on those who betrayed him. What follows is over six hundred pages of elaborate and complex scheming in which the Comte of Monte-Cristo settles accounts with those who betrayed him. The whole exercise is richly comical. His noble pedigree is obviously of the worst quality and his manners are that of a rank parvenu. Despite all the danger signs, the victims are all taken in by the Comte who baits his traps with diabolical brilliance. Before being finally snared, each victim approaches the Comte for advice. The Comte dutifully advises the victim of the danger but the victim can never resist the bait and everyone is snared. All the evil-doers meet their nemesis. <br /><br />Unlike many of Dumas' heroes who die alone and in tragic fashion, the Comte finds love and contentment at the end. Read and enjoy this book. It is a great story of how a nice guy gets the happy ending he so richly deserves. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14852617493222649673" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText17013278163762579176" style="display:none"><p>Despite its daunting length (around 1550 pages), Monte Cristo is a thoroughly enthralling novel and a genuine masterpiece. Filled with various adventures and several vignettes about French (especially Parisian) life in the upper classes in the first half of the 19th century, it relates the story of Edmond DantÃ¨s, a merchant sailor, who was falsely imprisoned on accusations of conspiring for the return of Napoleon in 1815. His sojourn in the ChÃ¢teau dâ€™If gaol leads to a spectacular reversal of fortune and provides him a platform to mount a spectacular revenge he later inflicted on those who contributed to his jailing. The plot in its itself is quite extraordinary and almost unbelievable. Definitely a classic and hard to put down.</p><br /></span>

<div id="review_72639914" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/72639914" />
    <a title="Pick Wick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2777425-pick-wick"><img alt="Pick Wick" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1406654893p2/2777425.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/72639914?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pick Wick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pick Wick" href="/user/show/2777425-pick-wick">Pick Wick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2777425-pick-wick?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2777425-pick-wick?shelf=french">french</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2777425-pick-wick?shelf=novels">novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2777425-pick-wick?shelf=19th-century">19th-century</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer72639914" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8180835665319387685">An extremely long story but it can very conveniently be separated into two parts (the "Edmond Dantès" section and the "Count of Monte-Cristo" one) and be read individually or at least not consecutively. The pervious events are repeatedly and pleasantly reminded to the reader throughout the book.<br/><br/>The two parts do not only happen during a totally different period of the main character's life but also deal with very distinctive themes. It is a wonderful and highly entertaining novel, with a lot of a</span>
  <span id="freeText8180835665319387685" style="display:none">An extremely long story but it can very conveniently be separated into two parts (the "Edmond Dantès" section and the "Count of Monte-Cristo" one) and be read individually or at least not consecutively. The pervious events are repeatedly and pleasantly reminded to the reader throughout the book.<br /><br />The two parts do not only happen during a totally different period of the main character's life but also deal with very distinctive themes. It is a wonderful and highly entertaining novel, with a lot of adventures, intrigues, suspense, revelations and romance. The quality of the text is enhanced by numerous pauses between those action scenes while the characters reflect on their lives. They draw the reader into their philosophical analysis and encourage him/her to ponder on the purpose of their own lives. Over so many pages, every major question/feeling is tackled: despair, revenge, fear, despite, ultimate power, good vs. bad, generosity, reward, cowardice, greed, loyalty, friendship, love etc.<br /><br />Dumas' prose is extremely agreeable and offers exquisite images for the reader to imagine. The precise description of the cities (Marseille, Paris, Rome etc), the magical rock of Monte-Cristo, the romantic stories of the Italian outlaws, the exotic and oriental mysteries brought into the elegant Parisian society and the very difficult French political atmosphere of the beginning of the 19th century – historically perfectly accurate –, all these elements of the story work like a time machine, transporting the reader into another world of refinery and enchantment but still reminding him/her that the cruel and haunting reality is never very far.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8180835665319387685" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3461720155" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3461720155" />
    <a title="Emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52528782-emma"><img alt="Emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582812346p2/52528782.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3461720155?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma" href="/user/show/52528782-emma">Emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3461720155" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4799024924839408687">4.5/5<br/><br/>After spending years hearing about this book, I first watch the German musical of The Count of Monte Cristo and got really intrigued by the story. The size of this novel impressed me, but, in the end, there is so much suspense that you do not see time pass and it is not tedious as the chapters are quite small. The language was not complicated considering the time period in which it was written and yet beautiful. Dumas is an impressive storyteller and it gave me the wish to read his other wo</span>
  <span id="freeText4799024924839408687" style="display:none">4.5/5<br /><br />After spending years hearing about this book, I first watch the German musical of The Count of Monte Cristo and got really intrigued by the story. The size of this novel impressed me, but, in the end, there is so much suspense that you do not see time pass and it is not tedious as the chapters are quite small. The language was not complicated considering the time period in which it was written and yet beautiful. Dumas is an impressive storyteller and it gave me the wish to read his other works. The characters are very interesting, well-constructed and complex. They all have multiple layers and evolve throughout the novel. I am very glad I decided to pick up this classic story about love and revenge that really deserves its praises.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4799024924839408687" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14784247664717415736">I read the full version, in French, and listened to an abridged audiobook version read by Bill Homewood, in English, just to make sure I didn't miss any details. (My French is a little rusty).<br/><br/>Audiobook version: The reading was well-done, but the text being read was so abbreviated you basically just ended up with the highlights.   <span id="freeText14784247664717415736" style="display:none">I read the full version, in French, and listened to an abridged audiobook version read by Bill Homewood, in English, just to make sure I didn't miss any details. (My French is a little rusty).<br /><br />Audiobook version: The reading was well-done, but the text being read was so abbreviated you basically just ended up with the highlights. Whole suspense-filled chapters became a short sentence or two.<br /><br />Full version: In one sense this is a horrible choice to read in a language you haven't spoken in years, just because it's so very long. On the other hand, aside from a couple slow sections, it's a real page-turner.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer238279900" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9742064987152280900">This is our December Book Club choice but I'd ordered it ahead and have just finished it. It was quite good though I was a bit confused near the ending with all the different names. I had to keep reminding myself that this was published in 1846. Reading The Greater Journey before this book helped with descriptions. That was interesting to me, the connections between the fiction of the era and the history book written this year. I'm glad this book was chosen as I'd never have read it, otherwise.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('m/FAJ/xbZS1PZ0P1CstMzGE4GQv6rGFM/WP8xB4Zxp388orfIbeECpaCaG/WN1Z/6uuK7XX7IYjTA3gsyjbyPA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('DyoHZ3IxXzjMp9FNRI5TUjP88w5ubqoo6HaGvk0j3AJoKc2fr92+HxVC+teYcknhuC9g6OE56uzGFgJWmQzoow==')})
  }

Young, attractive and very ambitious, George Duroy, known to his admirers as Bel-Ami, is offered a job as a journalist on La Vie francaise and soon makes a great success of his new career. But he also comes face to face with the realities of the corrupt society in which he lives - the sleazy colleagues, the manipulative mistresses, and wily financiers - and swiftly learns to become an arch-seducer, blackmailer and social climber in a world where love is only a means to an end. Written when Maupassant was at the height of his powers, &quot;Bel-Ami&quot; is a novel of great frankness and cynicism, but it is also infused with the sheer joy of life - depicting the scenes and characters of Paris in the belle epoque with wit, sensitivity, and humanity. Douglas Parmee\'s translation captures all the vigour and vitality of Maupassant\'s novel. His introduction explores the similarities between Bel-Ami and Maupassant himself and demonstrates the skill with which the author depicts his large cast of characters and the French society of the <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3679846833069617245"><i>This note regards <b>Alexandre Dumas, père</b>, the father of Alexandre Dumas, fils (son). For the son, see <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3186713.Alexandre_Dumas_fils' title='Alexandre Dumas fils' rel='nofollow noopener'>Alexandre Dumas fils</a>.</i><br/><br/>Alexandre Dumas, père (French for "father", akin to Senior in English), born Dumas Davy de la Pailleterie, was a French writer, best known for his numerous historical novels of high adventure which have made him one of the most widely read French authors in the world. Many of h</span>
  <span id="freeText3679846833069617245" style="display:none"><i>This note regards <b>Alexandre Dumas, père</b>, the father of Alexandre Dumas, fils (son). For the son, see <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3186713.Alexandre_Dumas_fils" title="Alexandre Dumas fils" rel="nofollow noopener">Alexandre Dumas fils</a>.</i><br /><br />Alexandre Dumas, père (French for "father", akin to Senior in English), born Dumas Davy de la Pailleterie, was a French writer, best known for his numerous historical novels of high adventure which have made him one of the most widely read French authors in the world. Many of his novels, including <i>The Count of Monte Cristo</i>, <i>The Three Musketeers</i>, <i>The Man in the Iron Mask</i>, and <i>The Vicomte de Bragelonne</i> were serialized. Dumas also wrote plays and magazine articles, and was a prolific correspondent.<br /><br />Dumas was of Haitian descent and mixed-race. His father, General Thomas-Alexandre Dumas Davy de la Pailleterie, was born in the French colony of Saint-Domingue (present-day Haiti) to Alexandre Antoine Davy de la Pailleterie, a French nobleman, and Marie-Cessette Dumas, a black slave. At age 14 Thomas-Alexandre was taken by his father to France, where he was educated in a military academy and entered the military for what became an illustrious career.<br /><br />Dumas's father's aristocratic rank helped young Alexandre Dumas acquire work with Louis-Philippe, Duke of Orléans, then as a writer, finding early success. He became one of the leading authors of the French Romantic Movement, in Paris.<br /><br /><i>Excerpted from <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexandre_Dumas,_p%C3%A8re" rel="nofollow noopener">Wikipedia</a></i>.</span>
